258→\n   259→void ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream(ActiveStream& stream, bool check_for_deferred_close) {\n   260→  // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\n   261→  // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n   262→  // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n   263→  // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n   264→  // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n   265→  // deleted first.\n   266→  bool reset_stream = false;\n   267→  // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. being notified of the\n   270→  // Envoy-internal stream instance being ended.\n   271→  if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n   272→      (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\n   273→       !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_)) {\n   274→    // Indicate local is complete at this point so that if we reset StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionTermination))) {\n   289→      stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\n   290→    } else {\n   291→ \"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_ignore_upstream_reason\")) {\n   297→        stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\n   298→      } else if stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\n   301→      } else {\n   302→        stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::LocalReset);\n   303→      }\n   304→    }\n   305→    reset_stream = true;\n   306→  }\n   307→\n   308→  if (!reset_stream) {\n We first see\n  // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n  // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n  // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n  // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n  // deleted first.\n  bool reset_stream = false;\n  // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01A3mpvmNKhf1L1h8TbgTN8d","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01YB2Q1L26Nth2C8RFtMoiUx","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is a critical component in Envoy's HTTP processing pipeline, responsible for routing, filter execution, stream lifecycle management, and response handling. Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` against `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` reveals **5 significant untested code paths** that handle edge cases, error conditions, and complex state transitions. These gaps could allow subtle bugs in stream lifecycle management, premature reset detection, codec error handling, and connection drain logic to slip through undetected.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Zombie Stream Lifecycle and Codec Completion Race Condition\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~2137-2180 (onCodecEncodeComplete, onCodecLowLevelReset), ~348-352 (canDestroyStream check in doDeferredStreamDestroy)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  When a stream's response encoding completes, the HCM checks if the stream is a \"zombie\" (marked for destruction but waiting for codec completion signal). The zombie stream path handles two codec completion scenarios: `onCodecEncodeComplete()` and `onCodecLowLevelReset()`. The code defers stream destruction until the codec signals completion, but the interaction between these states and the deferred close logic (`checkForDeferredClose()` with `close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag) is never directly tested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ZombieStreamOnCodecEncodeComplete`\n  - Setup: Create a stream, trigger `doEndStream()` before codec completes encoding (via response encoder still present but conditions met), verify stream becomes zombie\n  - Action: Simulate codec completion via `onCodecEncodeComplete()`\n  - Assertions:\n    - Stream is removed from active streams list\n    - `connection_manager_.close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag respected\n    - Connection deferred close triggered if flag enabled\n    - Stats: `downstream_cx_delayed_close_timeout_` incremented if applicable\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Zombie streams represent a subtle race condition where the HCM decides to end a stream before the codec has finished encoding the response. Untested zombies could lead to: (1) streams not being properly cleaned up, (2) double-destruction crashes, (3) connections remaining open when they should close, (4) resource leaks in long-lived connections.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Premature Stream Reset Detection and Connection Drain Logic\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~677-698 (isPrematureRstStream), ~702-749 (maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  The HCM detects \"premature resets\" (requests that complete without a response within a configured time threshold). When too many premature resets occur on a connection, the HCM triggers a connection drain via GOAWAY. The detection logic reads runtime configuration keys `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey` and `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey`. The drain decision involves three runtime-dependent thresholds: stream lifetime, total stream count, and reset-to-total ratio. The recursive guard flag `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents stack overflow but is never tested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureResetThresholdTriggersDrain`\n  - Setup:\n    - Configure runtime: `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 10`, `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 1`\n    - Create 5 streams that reset before 1 second lifetime (half ratio threshold)\n  - Action:\n    - Trigger 6th premature reset to exceed 50% threshold (6 * 2 > 10)\n    - Call `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`\n  - Assertions:\n    - GOAWAY sent to client (drain sequence started)\n    - `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat incremented\n    - `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag set to prevent recursion\n    - Subsequent calls to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` exit early\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Premature reset detection is a DoS defense mechanism. Untested code could: (1) fail to detect abusive patterns (allowing amplification attacks), (2) trigger false positives and unnecessarily drain healthy connections, (3) cause infinite recursion in edge cases (though guarded against), (4) allow requests to complete without proper accounting if the recursive guard fails.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Deferred Request Processing with Mixed Deferred States\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~2533-2563 (ActiveStream::onDeferredRequestProcessing), ~2565-2604 (ConnectionManagerImpl::onDeferredRequestProcessing with reverse iteration)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When the HCM receives more than `max_requests_per_io_cycle` requests in a single dispatch cycle, subsequent requests are deferred to the next I/O iteration to prevent starvation. The deferred state is complex: headers, data, trailers, and metadata can each be independently deferred. The `onDeferredRequestProcessing()` method must reconstruct the proper sequence (headers → metadata → data → trailers) while tracking end_stream flags correctly. The connection-level function iterates streams in reverse order and dynamically adjusts iteration if streams are removed.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `DeferredRequestProcessingMetadataInterleaved`\n  - Setup:\n    - Configure `max_requests_per_io_cycle = 1`\n    - Mock codec to generate: Request1 (headers+data), Request2 (headers), Request3 (headers+metadata+trailers)\n  - Action:\n    - Dispatch all in single onData call (triggers deferred for Request2 and Request3)\n    - Simulate next I/O cycle calling `onDeferredRequestProcessing()`\n  - Assertions:\n    - Request2: Headers sent to filter manager with end_stream=true\n    - Request3: Headers → metadata → trailers sent in correct order\n    - All three requests have `deferred_to_next_io_iteration_` flag cleared\n    - Filter manager receives calls in exact sequence\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Deferred processing is critical for fairness in high-throughput scenarios.
